I listened to this video the other day & mulled over as to whether adding my two cents worth, $8.85 in today's money.

But anyway, no, there were no iterations to the V1 drawing we decided to make public I recall. My build for example is V17 & that was to a point that I felt everything geled together & still stands up today, in terms of how subassemblies & measures work out.

The public drawing is a great 'kick-off' point for builders to at least get a handle on the miniatures dimensions. As said, its up to the builder to tweak it further, if a more push towards accuracy is wanted. And remember, no replica is fully 100% accurate to the original, something will always never match precisely, no matter how small the detail!.

My rule in terms of blueprints, is:

1) never trust someone else's blueprint, and

2) never trust your own blueprint!.

Its never been a better time for budding Falcon builders to, um, build a replica!.

New ID's found here by keen eyes are adding to all the sheer hard slog done over decades by others, many that remain unknown to the current wave of builders here, but they were there, in the trenches & have passed on their knowledge generously.

Parts maps, forums, parts offered, folks still accessible that know a wealth of Falcon knowledge, its all there!. Obviously the drawing has its errors, the cockpit diameter for example, thats another story all in itself on my part & of course, serious builders now know its correct diameter.

Stu

Post #668  (forum post #5680928)
Author    : Studio Kitbash
Date      : Nov 17, 2025 at 4:19 PM
Reactions : Like, Haha — Shamon, joberg, eagle1
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Studio Kitbash Rules for Accuracy:

Build to 1/10th of a millimeter of accuracy, reverse engineering from the greeblies.

That way, if you are off by a factor of 100, you are still within 1cm of proximity to perfection.  Below 2mm I would say is not noticeable to the naked eye.

Is the original Falcon 170cm, or is it 169.25cm, or is it 173cm?  These are THREE officially "correct" answers to the question, and that's just "the ones I know about."

Or is it NONE of these three, and you'll never know, until you build two of them -- one to get it wrong, and one to achieve accuracy by?

The answer is:  I'm not telling.

...

But only because:  I don't know either.

But when I do find it, I'll give you my opinion, and you can betcha sweet bottle of Shiraz that I'll also be wrong, according to at least three other self-appointed experts.

Patience, young Padawan?

No, what's required is perseverance, balls of titanium, and indifference to any mathematical answers that aren't derived from you doing the work yourself from original greeblies or castings.  To your own satisfaction.  To your own ability to withstand the opinion, contradiction, bullying, or mocking of anyone else.

You trusting someone else's numbers = You being royally screwed by your own laziness.  Sorry, but there's no way to do it but the hard way.  If you haven't learned this lesson the hard way, you will soon.

You can be confident that a fair amount of RPF information is disinformation or misinformation (whether intentional or not), as everyone wants to have the only actually accurate Falcon out there.

And mine is also imperfect, between at least 1/10th of a millimeter to 1 cm.

You just have to accept what your allowable tolerances are.  Remember that you are spending ten years to replicate something that was built in 3-6 months, and that at a certain point, no matter what, everyone gets to the point of saying, "that's close enough."

So RealDaveWinter, like EACH AND ANY OF US currently building one, only gets to decrease the spread of his allowable tolerance to below 1cm because of public admissions of error on the build threads of those who have gone before, and THAT is the real lesson of this micro-drama, each and every time it comes up, which is itself on a fairly regular schedule now.

But that being said, RealDaveWinter your two Olsa caliper logo greeblies (Tamiya 1/35 M8 Armored Car part #9, circular-with-inner-hexagon greeblies, X2)  on bottom left of your lower landing gear box are spread apart too much by at least 1mm if not 2-3mm, and should be brought closer together.  You've got the two greeblies far enough apart that if you had a third identical greeblie, it would fit in between them.  On the real ship, according to Chronicles pictures, the distance from lower outer diameter rim of the top greeblie to upper outer diameter rim of the bottom greeblie is not quite enough to accommodate a third greeblie, by a very specific amount that your calipers will tell you.

But that's just my eye, and ahem, I could be wrong...

I didn't put anyone down, if anything, I praised their work, including yours. Maybe you missed that.

- I mention that I was told the drawings were not correct.

- I mention the issues I noticed right away, including the cockpit tube (which I think you specifically called out)

- I mention I'm using a very old revision and that there are probably new ones out there (which there apparently are, but hidden away)

- I state that "the three folks that worked on the drawings I have done an amazing job." And I commented on how it was such a great job given how the information was gleamed from old magazine photos.

- I mention that the final results were only off by a quarter of an inch here and there, which is amazing.

- But yes, I do mention the items that were not correct, because;

    a. it's perfectly acceptable to mention things that are not correct. (especially given that everyone involved apparently already knows this)

    b. discovering those incorrect things, and how they were addressed, work around, or skipped over, is part of the story of the build. It's part of the process.

- I said that the issues became a problem for me because of my goals.

- At several other points I mention other issues I ran into with the drawings because it was relevant to the area I was speaking about.

I do not see anything in those statements that is offensive.

Be that as it may Stu, pointing out an error is not bad form. People do that to me every single freaking day.

[Edit]

Updated after finding the exact wording. Apologies again to Stuart
		

Click to expand...

Dave, on reflection, I will offer my apologies to you. My rant was simply pointless & really didn't warrant me saying anything to rock the boat!. Sometimes with 'passion' projects such as the Falcon, its too easy to slip into almost an alter ego of oneself & not see clearly the intentions of others, if something is said, taken in the wrong context, its all too easy to fly off the handle & upset others, as I see has happened here with me, towards you & others have now seen & upset also.

Your replica build is wonderful Dave, just keep pushing it to the finish line & updating with your video series, the masses love seeing the trials & tribulations of just what it takes to build. Humbling on my part, to see the use of my dome set successfully implemented here as well!.

Sincere apologies again Dave.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Started dry fitting the mandible bays.

One of the challenges with this is that the edges of the armour plates, on top and bottom, line up with, and intersect with, specific greeblies in the mechanical bays, but you also can't really align the mechanical bays properly until you have the edges of the armour plates to line them up with. So it's a little chicken and egg race here.

[IMAGE: https://www.therpf.com/forums/attachments/1765132787248-png.1995660/]

Post #688  (forum post #5707286)
Author    : Searun
Date      : Mar 10, 2026 at 6:32 PM
Reactions : Like — joberg
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Dave,

I will look harder to see if a specific problem can be spotted.

 In the interim, the Falcon puzzle arrangement taught me to look for “white space” between some of the greeblies that could be readily compressed to make up the delta to fit the as-built structure. Obviously, when kit parts touch each other you become grid locked. But that fact can often suggest a fix. The engine deck drove me crasy until I first built modules of connecting greeblies to shift around. If that does not help, structure needs some rework. Bottom line as you well know, kit parts determine the dimensions. The Falcon is wonky.

Post #690  (forum post #5707326)
Author    : eagle1
Date      : Mar 11, 2026 at 1:41 AM
Reactions : Like — Searun, joberg
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi Dave. 

My mandible sidewall length measure, from very front, to the start of the M36 tall grill kit part, is 756mm. The M36 part doesn't sit on the mandible plate as such, rather, it acts as a spacer between the mandible plate end & sidewall casting. The end of the mandible wall is quite thick to where its cut off, at least 4mm, thats why the M36 part looks sunken in between the plate & casting. 

Hope that helps a little.

Stu

View attachment 2018071

Click to expand...

Dave,

Most likely if you are "too long" it indicates your hull diameter is off, but which can usually easily be solved by adding strips of Plastruct card stock of 1-2mm depth until you are satisfied.

But the technical answer to your question, "I cannot see what I've done wrong" is very easy to answer:  You've only done it ONCE.  You're not really building a Millennium Falcon until/unless you're on your 2nd, 3rd, and 4th attempts at any given area.  In my own case, I've gotten to SEVEN and am still thinking of doing it over to get it "just right."

So hang in there -- she's a fickle mistress, and yet she demands your loyalty.  

BTW, your sidewall looks flawless and beautiful and amazing, and makes a nice reference picture for my own collection, so thanks for that.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

For my pod project, which is in metric though it's 1/6 size of an imperial design, I ended up making a table and having it handy all the time! Does this help?

[IMAGE: APaQ0SQNcutsazYDia0zHsU3I7F9cMJ04Dny2g_F3UOl924fizqPOprzdSyqirGf0_UblrO-Sgbx9Pbj2yF-WsCBAO7te1b7THVLz-18B-Z62hDIozCZDqDjARTJu9OXUYbJ-dGtgcRpY5SZBYAs9nOYRREFm9THRYFkKOCaCpCIDnN9LD4qIpI8wW5l9sI=w16383]

						Useful metric conversions
					

I’ve been having to do a lot of fiddly metric conversions for recent projects. The problem is that conventions for small (sub inch) imperial measurements are often an incoherent mess; a mix of fractions and decimal values. Woodworkers tend to use fractions for easy halving and use of a tape
